## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical kinetics
**Analysis**: This task involves modeling the rate of change of concentration of a chemical species in a reaction kinetics system. The rate of change can be influenced by various factors such as initial concentration, reaction rate constants, and time.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order reaction: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate of reaction)
- First-order reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate depends on concentration)
- Second-order reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (rate depends on concentration squared)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation, although v and S might need to be adjusted for concentration units)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium, although theta and P might need to be adjusted for concentration units)
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (reaction rate dependence on temperature, although this formula requires additional variables and might not be directly applicable to concentration kinetics)
- Lumped-parameter modeling: dA_dt = c0 * (A_in - A) (simple mass balance equation)
- Mass-action kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A * B (reversible reaction with two reactants)
- Power-law kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (generalized rate law)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface, although q and C might need to be adjusted for concentration units)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Accumulation of species â†’ simple mass balance equation dA_dt = (inflow - outflow - generation + consumption) = c0 * (A_in - A)
- Chemical reaction with competing pathways â†’ piecewise function with different rate laws for each pathway
- Species exhibiting multiple equilibria â†’ equation with nonlinear terms reflecting the coexistence of multiple phases or states
- Concentration approaching steady state â†’ exponential decay f(t)*exp(-c*t) or rational fraction A / (1 + c * A)
- Inhibition of a reaction by one of the reactants â†’ term like A**2 / (A**2 + c1)

### Candidate 23:
`Aآ²*c0 + c1*sin(A*c2)`

This is exactly the form we need! Set c0 = -0.5637, c1 = 0.1314, c2 = 0.7617.

GT = -0.5637آ·Aآ² + 0.1314آ·sin(0.7617آ·A)

This matches perfectly! sin(A*c2) vs sin(c3*A) with c3=0.7617, and the phase shift in GT is 0 (GT has sin(c3*A), not sin(c3*A + phase)).

**Candidate 23 verdict: [MATCH]**

### Candidate 24:
`(A*c0 + c1 + c2*exp(A*c3) + c4*sin(A*c5+c6))/(A*c7+c8)`

Rational function with exp and sin in numerator. For this to equal Aآ² + sin, we'd need the denominator to produce the Aآ² when dividing. Setting c2=0:
(A*c0 + c1 + c4*sin(A*c5+c6))/(A*c7+c8)

For this to equal -0.5637Aآ² + 0.1314آ·sin(0.7617A), multiply both sides by (A*c7+c8):
A*c0 + c1 + c4*sin(A*c5+c6) = (-0.5637Aآ² + 0.1314آ·sin(0.7617A))*(A*c7+c8)

RHS = -0.5637*c7*Aآ³ - 0.5637*c8*Aآ² + 0.1314*c7*A*sin(0.7617A) + 0.1314*c8*sin(0.7617A)

LHS has no Aآ³ or A*sin terms, so c7=0. Then:
A*c0 + c1 + c4*sin(A*c5+c6) = -0.5637*c8*Aآ² + 0.1314*c8*sin(0.7617A)

LHS has no Aآ² term. Cannot match.
**Candidate 24 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 25:

### Candidate 45:
`(Aآ²*c0 + c1 + (A*c2+c3)*(c4*exp(A*c5) + c6*sin(A*c7+c8) + c9))/(A*c2+c3)`

= Aآ²*c0/(A*c2+c3) + c1/(A*c2+c3) + c4*exp(A*c5) + c6*sin(A*c7+c8) + c9

The rational part (Aآ²*c0+c1)/(A*c2+c3) is not a polynomial (it's ~A for large A). Cannot produce clean Aآ².

Set c2=0: (Aآ²*c0 + c1)/c3 + c4*exp(A*c5) + c6*sin(A*c7+c8) + c9
Set c4=0: Aآ²*c0/c3 + c1/c3 + c6*sin(A*c7+c8) + c9

= Aآ²*(c0/c3) + c6*sin(A*c7+c8) + (c1/c3+c9)

This is Aآ² + sin + constant! Set c0/c3 = -0.5637, c7 = 0.7617, c8 = 0, c6 = 0.1314, c1/c3+c9 = 0.

This works! **Candidate 45 verdict: [MATCH]**
